
# The Children

### 288 reprints from 1863-09-19 to 1899-12-30

## [The Children](http://chroniclingamerica.loc.gov/lccn/sn84038223/1864-09-22/ed-1/seq-4/)

#### by The Village Schoolmaster [Charles M. Dickinson]

#### From _Maysville weekly bulletin_

#### 1864-09-22

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me  
To bid me good night and be kissed;  
O! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck, in their tender embrace,  
O! the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face.  
  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last!  
Of love that my heart will remember  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin;  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
O! my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fount of my feelings will flow,  
When I think of the paths deep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them—  
Of the tempests of Fate blowing wild,  
O! there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy,  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses;  
His glory still gleams in their eyes;  
O! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild;  
And I know, now, how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
  
I ask not a life for the dear one  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayers would bound back to myself.  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge  
They have taught e the goodness of God;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness  
Where I shut the for breaking a rule,  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshhold no more;  
Ah! how shall I sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door!  
I shall miss the &quot;good-nights,&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning for me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve—  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons of life are all ended,  
And death says, &quot;The school is dismissed!&quot;  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed.  

</td></tr></table>

---

## [From _Grant County herald._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn85033133/1863-11-10/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1863-11-10 &middot; [Lancaster, Wis.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Lancaster%2C_Wisconsin)

THE CHILDREN.  
When the lessons and tasks are ended,  
tnd the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me  
To bid me good night and be kissed,  
Oh! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace:  
Oh! the &gt; miles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshide of love on my face.  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last.  
Of love that my heart will remember  
&lt; While it wakas tothe pulso of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin;  
When the ;*’ory of God was about me,  
And the &quot;glory of gladness within.  
Oh! my heart grows weak as a woman’s  
And the fount of ray feelings will flow,  
When I think of ths paths steep and stony  
Where the feet ol the dear ones must go;  
01 the mountains of sin hanging over thorn,  
Of the tempests of Fate, blowing wild—  
Oh! there’s nothing on e:v tb half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
There are idols of hearts a«d of households,  
There are angels of God in disg’-ise;  
His suuiight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eves  
Ob! these truants from homo and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know now how Jesus coaid liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayers would bound back to myself:  
Ab! a seraph may pray 1&lt; r a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended  
I have banished the rule and ihe rod;  
I have taught them the greatness cf knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness  
Where I shut them (or breaking a rule:  
My frown is sufficient for correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave ihe old house in autumn,  
To traverse the threshold no more;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That shall meet me each morn at the door!  
1 shall miss their “good night’’ and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning for me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve—  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons of life are all ended,  
And Death says, “The school is dismissed!”  
May the little ones gather around roe  
To bid me “Good night” and be kissed.

## [From _Sixpenny Magazine 1861-1868_](https://archive.org/details/sim_sixpenny-magazine_1865-08-01_10_4/page/n111/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1865-08-01 &middot; [London, England](http://dbpedia.org/resource/London)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

en sacred.  
  
  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
WueEN the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me  
To bid me “ Good-night,” and be kissed.  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace ;  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face.  
  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood—too lovely to last—  
Of joy that my heart will remember  
While it wakes to the pulse of the Past;  
Kre the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of Sorrow and Sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have donc ;  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun ;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil ;  
But my prayer would bound back to myself:  
Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door;  
  
I shall miss the “ Good-nights,” and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee ;  
  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
  
That are brought every morning for me.

## [From _The Catholic World, A Monthly Magazine of General Literature and Science (1865-1906)_](https://archive.org/details/sim_the-catholic-world-a-monthly-magazine_1865-10_2_7/page/n73/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1865-10-01 &middot; [New York](http://dbpedia.org/resource/New_York_City)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

.  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
WueEn the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me  
To bid me “good night,” and be kissed.  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace ;  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face.  
  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood—too lovely to last—  
  
Of joy that my heart will remember  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past :  
  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
I ask not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done ;  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun ;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil ;  
But my prayer would bound back to myself:  
Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner mast pray for himself.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To trayerse its threshold no more ;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door;  
I shall miss the “ good-nights ” and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee ;  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning for me.  
  
  
  
All-Hallow Eve ; or, The Test of Futurity.  
  
From The Lamp.  
  
ALL-HALLOW EVE; OR, THE TEST OF FUTURITY.

## [From _The daily phoenix._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn84027008/1865-10-04/ed-1/?sp=4)

#### 1865-10-04 &middot; [Columbia, S.C.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Columbia%2C_South_Carolina)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
The Children. &#x27;

The Children.  
BY CHARLES DICKINSON.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
J.nd tbe school for the day is dismissed,

To bid me good night and be kissed ;  
Ob ! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace,

Where the feet of the dear ones must go ;

Hut my prayers would bound back to  
myself ;

1 have banished the rule and the rod ;  
I huve taught them the goodness of knowl­  
edge,

Where I shut them for breaking a rule ;

## [From _Marshall County Republican._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn84038034/1866-06-21/ed-1/?sp=4)

#### 1866-06-21 &middot; [Plymouth, Ind.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Plymouth%2C_Indiana)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
THB CHILBrE.  
  
BY CHArLES DICrIYSON.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me  
To bid me good night and be kissed;  
Oh! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace,  
Oh! the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face.  
And, when they are gone, I sit dreaming,  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last,  
Of love that my heart will remember  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
E&#x27;er the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of soorrow and sin;  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh! my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s  
And the fount of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths seep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild.  
Oh! there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses;  
His glory still gleams in their eyes;  
Oh! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild:  
And I know, noow, how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayers would bound back to myself,  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness  
Where I shut them for breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficiont correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the house in autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door?  
I shall miss the &quot;good nights&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning for me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at even  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons of life are ended,  
And death says: &quot;Thy school is dismissed!&quot;  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed.  
A TEAAS NORTHIER.  
Where it Comes Fro

The Children..  
  
BY CHARLES DICKENS.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended;  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
  
The little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed ;  
  
QO! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace,  
  
O! the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face  
  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past.  
  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A. partaer of sorrow and sin ;  
  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
9! my heart-grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountain of feelings will flow  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them—  
Of the tempests of Fate blowing wild,  
O! there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
  
They&#x27;re the idols of hearts and of households  
They&#x27;re the angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses ;  
His glory still beams in their eyes.  
O! those truants from home and from Heaven  
They have made me more manly and mild!  
And I know now, how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.

All radient, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
T would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself:  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.

## [From _The Columbian._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn83032011/1866-07-28/ed-1/?sp=4)

#### 1866-07-28 &middot; [Bloomsburg, Pa.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Bloomsburg%2C_Pennsylvania)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

THE CHILDrEN.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me  
To bid me &quot;Good-night&quot; and be kissed;  
Oh, the little arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace;  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of Heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face.  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
of my childhood--too lonely to last  
Of joy that my heart will remember  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All-radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
I shall leave the old house in the Autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door;  
I shall miss the &quot;Good-nights,&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning for me.  
  
AGRICULTURAL.  
Buckwheat  
The value of this crop should insure  
it a better treatment than it usually re­  
ceives from the generality of cultivators.  
So
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://tile.loc.gov/image-services/iiif/service:ndnp:pst:batch_pst_carnegie_ver01:data:sn83032011:00237287964:1866072801:0318/pct:7.832639,9.506636,12.869324,19.648009/!600,600/0/default.jpg"/>

## [From _West-Jersey pioneer._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn83032103/1868-07-03/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1868-07-03 &middot; [Bridgeton, N.J.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Bridgeton%2C_New_Jersey)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
When the tasks and the lessons are ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me  
To bid me good night and be kissed ;  
Oh ! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in the ir tender embrace;  
Oh! the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
Oh 1 my heart grows as weak as a woman’s,  
And the fount of my feelings will flow,  
”hen I think of the paths steep and stony,  
y* here the teat of the dear ones must go ;  
Ol the mountains of sin hanging o’er them—  
Of the tempeits of fate blowing wild,  
For there’s nothing on earth half so holy,  
As the innocent heart of a child!

I have banished the rule and the rod ;  
1 have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God ;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them for breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet each morn at the door!  
I shall miss the good nights and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innoseut glee;  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning for me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at even—  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their pattering feet,

## [From _The Conservative._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn87075001/1868-08-27/ed-1/?sp=2)

#### 1868-08-27 &middot; [M'connelsville, Ohio](http://dbpedia.org/resource/McConnelsville%2C_Ohio)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
THE CHIILDREN.  
  
nY Charles DicKens  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed;  
Ol the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace;  
Of the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face.  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A par tner of sorrow and sin;  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Ol my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempest of Fate blowing wild;  
Of there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
They are idols of hearts and of households;  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses;  
His glory still gleams in their eyes.  
Of those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild!  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The Kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done;  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the wisdom of God;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness;  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction;  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones,  
That mect me each morn at the door!  
I shall miss the &quot;good nights&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet  
When the lessons are all ended,  
And Death says, &quot;The school is dismissed!&quot;  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed.

## [From _Sunbury American._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn84026403/1868-11-21/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1868-11-21 &middot; [Sunbury, Pa.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Sunbury%2C_Pennsylvania)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

 everywhere  
Do not forget to examins tell the articl you bny, in  
order to ge te gonuine,  
  
PoETICAL.  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
DY CHARLES DiCKeNS.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather round me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed.  
O! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace;  
O! the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face.  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past.  
Ere the world and its wickodness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin;  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
O! my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones mustgo;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Or the tempest of Fate blowing wild;  
O! there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
There are idols of hearts and of households;  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses;  
His glory still gleams in their eyes.  
O! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild!  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The Kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not a life for the dear ones.  
All radiant, as others have done;  
But that I may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner.  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rufe and the rod,  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
When I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is a sufficient correction;  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each hour at the door!  
I shall miss the &quot;good-nights&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons are all ended,  
And Death says, &quot;The school is dismissed!&quot;  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed!
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://tile.loc.gov/image-services/iiif/service:ndnp:pst:batch_pst_deike_ver01:data:sn84026403:0028077604A:1868112101:0748/pct:16.174902,14.912281,24.155706,79.331140/!600,600/0/default.jpg"/>

</tr></table>

## [From _Ashtabula weekly telegraph._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn83035216/1869-01-09/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1869-01-09 &middot; [Ashtabula, Ohio](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Ashtabula%2C_Ohio)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

ur love for each other.  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
BY CHARLEs DICKENS.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather round me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
oly neck in a tender embrncc e  
h, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remnember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past  
Ere the world and its wickedness met  
A partner of sorrow and sin;  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempest ofFase blowing wild;  
Oh, there is hothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a&#x27;child!  
They Ate idols of hearts and of hodscholds,  
They areangels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes;  
Oh  
those truants from home and from heaven.  
Thry have gade metmore manly and mild!  
And I know how, Jesns can liken&quot;  
e kingom of o to a child  
I ask pot a life for the lear ones,  
All rediant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray to God to guard them from evil,  
but my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner may pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodnes of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah, how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door!  
I shall miss the &quot;good nights&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee  
The groups on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn, and at evening  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And death says, &quot;The school is dismissed!&#x27;  
May the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good night and be kissed.

<img alt="Page image" src="https://tile.loc.gov/image-services/iiif/service:ndnp:ohi:batch_ohi_guildenstern_ver01:data:sn83035216:00280775186:1869010901:0015/pct:31.689273,49.295775,12.330456,33.338028/!600,600/0/default.jpg"/>

## [From _The Union and journal._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn83009571/1869-01-22/ed-1/?sp=1)

oetry.  
THE ChIFTrEN.  
The following beautiful poem was written by  
Charles Dickens:  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed:  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past.  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin;  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go!  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempest of sin blowing wild;  
Oh! there is nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disgulse;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes:  
Oh! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild!  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The Kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not a life of the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
Hat that life may have just enough shadows  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule!  
My frown is sufficient correction;  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shal

But my prayer would bound back to myself;

But a sinner must pray for himself.

have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
srey have taught me the goodness of God;

My love it the law of the school.

Ah, how I sha I sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door!

And the gush of their innocent glee,

by Charles Dickens.]

My neek in tender embrace I

Ere the world and its wickedness made me   
A partner of sorrow and sin;   
Whea the glory of God was about me,   
And the glory of gladness within.

## [From _The Kenosha telegraph._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn85033123/1869-01-28/ed-1/?sp=6)

#### 1869-01-28 &middot; [Kenosha, Wis.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Kenosha%2C_Wisconsin)

 darkness,   
Where I shut them for breaking a rule;   
My frown is sufficient correction—   
My love is the law of the school.   
1 shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traversits threshold no more ;   
Ah. how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each day at the door!   
I shall miss the “good nights” and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,   
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.   
I shall miss them at morn and evening,  
Their song in the school and the street;   
I ehall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.   
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And death says, “The school is dismissed!”   
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed.

## [From _Friends' Intelligencer (1853-1910)_](https://archive.org/details/sim_friends-intelligencer_1869-07-17_26_20/page/n12/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1869-07-17 &middot; [Philadelphia](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Philadelphia)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

_  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
BY CHARLES DICKENS.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me,  
  
To bid me good-night and be kissed :  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace !  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face !  
  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last ;  
  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin ;  
  
When the glory of God was atout me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman’s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go ;  
  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempest of Fate blowing wild ;  
  
Oh! there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households ;  
They are angels of God in disguise ;  
  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes ;  
  
Oh ! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild!  
  
And I know how Jesus could liken .  
The Kingdom of God to a child.  
  
I ask nota life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun ;  
  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
  
But my prayer would bound back to myself ;  
Ab ! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
  
They have taught me the goodness of God ;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule ;  
My frown is sufficient correction ;  
  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more ;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones,  
That meet me each morn at the door !  
I shall miss the “ good-nights’’ and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
T
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://iiif.archive.org/image/iiif/2/sim_friends-intelligencer_1869-07-17_26_20%2Fsim_friends-intelligencer_1869-07-17_26_20_jp2.zip%2Fsim_friends-intelligencer_1869-07-17_26_20_jp2%2Fsim_friends-intelligencer_1869-07-17_26_20_0012.jp2/pct:6.067251,12.934028,68.347953,69.596354/,600/0/default.jpg"/>

The Kingdom of God to a child.

All radiant, as others have done ;  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah, a seraph may pray for sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod:  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the wisdom of God :—  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule ;  
My frown is sufficient correction ;  
My love is the law of the school.

## [From _The evening Argus._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn84038628/1869-12-20/ed-1/?sp=2)

#### 1869-12-20 &middot; [Rock Island, Ill.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Rock_Island%2C_Illinois)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

 free love  
eetrines is and out of the pulpit.  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
BY CHARLES DICKENS.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are haloes of heaven,  
hedding sunshine of love on my face.  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the path steep and stormy,  
Where the feet of the dead on ia mast go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempest of Fate blowing wild;  
Oh! there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
They are idols of hearts and of households;  
They are angels of God in disguise,  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes;  
Oh! thost truants from home and from heaven,  
They htve made me more manly and mild!  
And I kn w how Jesus could liken  
he Uingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not a life for the dead ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun,  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself,  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God,  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
When I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction;  
My love is the law of the school,  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones,  
That meet me each night at the door?  
I shall miss the good nights and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me,  
I shall
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://tile.loc.gov/image-services/iiif/service:ndnp:iune:batch_iune_article_ver01:data:sn84038628:00295879956:1869122001:0575/pct:8.434420,5.889571,23.616376,93.047035/!600,600/0/default.jpg"/>

= =  
  
  
  
For the Chilvren.  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones apes’ around me,  
  
To bid me good-night and be kissed :  
  
O! the little white arms that encircle  
  
My neck in a tender embrace :  
  
O! the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face.  
  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin :  
  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
O! my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and strong,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild ;  
  
O |! there is nothing on earth half so holy  
  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households ;  
They are angels of God in disguise ;  
  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
  
His glory still gleams in their eyes ;  
  
O! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild :  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
  
All radiant, as others have done,  
  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
  
I have banished the rule and the rod ;  
  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God ;  
My cent ig a dungeon of darkness,  
  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule ;  
  
My frown is sufficient correction ; ;  
  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
  
To traverse its threshold no more ;  
  
Ah! how { shall sigh for the dear ones,  
  
That meet me each morn at the door:  
  
I shall miss the “ good-nights ” and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
  
That are brought every morning to me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve,  
Their song in the school and the street ;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet;  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And Death says “ the school is dismissed ”  
re the little ones gather around me,  
  
bid me good-night and be kissed.  
  
Cuaritzes Dickens.

DT CHARLES DICKENS.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day Is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me,  
To hid me good-mght and be kissed;  
Oh. the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace I  
Oh, the smiles that are halos 01 heaven.  
Shedding sunshine ot lore on my face I  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remcmtier.  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin;  
When the glory of Oral was about me.  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s  
And the fountains of feeling will flow.  
When 1 think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them.  
Of the tempest of sin blowing wild;  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart or a child!  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disgnise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes:  
Oh, those truants from home and Irom heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mRd!  
And I know now how Jesus could likeu  
The Kiagdom of God to a child.  
I ask not a life of the dear ones.  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have Jost enough shadows  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But the prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,

## [From _The Phrenological Journal and Science of Health (1870-1911)_](https://archive.org/details/sim_phrenological-journal-and-science-of-health_1870-09_51_3/page/n33/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1870-09-01 &middot; [Philadelphia](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Philadelphia)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
Ou! my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will low  
  
When I think of the paths, steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild ;  
  
Oh! there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise ;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their treeses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes.  
Oh! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun.

. THE CHILDREN. BY  
CHARLES DICKENS. When the lessons and  
tasks are all ended. And the school for  
the day is dismissed, And the little  
Dues gather around me To bid me good  
night and be kissed ; Oh, the little  
white anna that encircle My neck in a  
tender embrace ! Oh, the smiles that are  
hales of heaven, Shedding sunshine of  
love on my face ! And when they are gone  
I sit dreaming Of my childhood too  
lovely to last; Of love that my heart  
will remember, When it wakes to the  
poise of the past, Ere the world and its  
wickedness made mo A. partner of sorrow  
and sin, When the glory of God was about  
me, And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and  
stony, Where the feet of the dear ones  
most go; Of the mountains of sin hanging  
o&#x27;er them, Of the tempest of Fate  
blowing wild; Oh ! there is nothing on  
earth half so holy As the innocant heart  
of a child ! They are idols of hearts  
and of households ; They are angels of  
God in disguise : His sunlight still  
sleeps in their tresses, His glory still  
gleams in their eyes; Oh ! those truants  
from home and from heaven, They have  
made me more manly and mild ! And I know  
how Jesus could liken The kingdom of God  
to a child. Seek not a life for the dear  
ones, All radiant, as others have done.  
Bat that life may have jost enough  
shadow To temper the glare of the son. I  
would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to  
myself. Ah ! a seraph may pray for a  
sinner. Bat a sinner must pray for  
himself. The twig is so easily broken, I  
have banished the rule and the rod ; I  
have taught them the goodness of  
knowledge ; They have taught me the  
goodness of God ; My heart is a dungeon  
of darkness, Where I shut them from  
breaking a rule; My frown is sufficient  
correction; My love is the law of the  
school. I shall leave the old house in  
the Autumn, To traverse its threshold no  
more; Ah ! how I shall sigh for the dear  
ones. That meet me each mom at the door!  
I shall miss the &quot; good nights &quot; and the  
kisses, And the gush of their innocent  
glee, The group on the green, and toe  
flowers That are brought every morning  
to me. I shall miss them at morn and at  
eve, Their song in the school and the  
street; I shall miss the low hum of

delicate feet. When the lessons and

## [From _Dodgeville chronicle._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn85033019/1871-01-20/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1871-01-20 &middot; [Dodgeville, Wis.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Dodgeville%2C_Wisconsin)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

embrace!  
Oh ! the smiles that are halos of heaven.  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember.  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past.  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh ! the heart grows weak as a woman’s.  
And the fountain of feeling will flow.  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them.  
Of Hie tempest of fate blowing wild;  
Oh! there is nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
They are idols of hearts and of households;  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses.  
His glory still gleams in their eyes;  
Oh ! these truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild;  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask hot a life for the dear ones.  
All radiant, as others have done.  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself:  
Ah ! a seraph may pray for a sinner.  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended;  
I have banished the rule and the rod :  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more,  
Ah ! how shall I sigh for the dear ones,  
That meet me each morn at the door!  
I shall miss the good nights and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve,  
Their song in the school and tho street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And death says, “ The school is dismissed l”  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed.

## [From _The home journal._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn95068565/1873-10-02/ed-1/?sp=1)

When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school of the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed;  
O the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace;

Shedding sunshine of love on my face.

They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses;  
His glory still gleams in their eyes.  
O those shouts from home and from Heaven,  
They liave made me more manly and mild!  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child,

But my prayer would bound back to myself,

But a sinner must pray for himself,

## [From _The Rock Island daily Argus._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn85034301/1873-10-25/ed-1/?sp=6)

#### 1873-10-25 &middot; [Rock Island, Ill.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Rock_Island%2C_Illinois)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dism  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good-night and be kissed;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
On, the smiles that are halos of heaven.  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember.  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made m  
A partner of sorrow and sin.  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths, steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them.  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild;  
Oh! there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
s the innocent heart of a child!  
They are idols of hearts and of households;  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
And his sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
And his glory still gleams in their eyes.  
Oh! those truants from home and from heave  
They have made me more manly and mild!  
And I know how our Saviour could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.

## [From _The Rock Island daily Argus._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn85034301/1873-10-25/ed-1/?sp=6)

#### 1873-10-25 &middot; [Rock Island, Ill.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Rock_Island%2C_Illinois)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

,  
I3ots TA, GAMaGE. M.D  
  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended.  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge  
They have taught me the goodness of God;  
My heart is a dungson of darkness,  
Where I shut them for breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction:  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the antumn.  
To traverse the threshold no more;  
Ah! how shail I sigh for the dear ones,  
That meet me each morn at the door;  
I shall miss the &quot;good nights&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at evening.  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voic  
And the pat of their delicate feer.  
When the lesson and tasks are all ended,  
And death says &quot;the school is dismissed  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed!

Oh, my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow.  
When I think of the paths, steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;

## [From _The Jeffersonian._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn84026399/1873-11-27/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1873-11-27 &middot; [Stroudsburg, Pa.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Stroudsburg%2C_Pennsylvania)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good-night and be kissed :  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face !  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
Oflove that my heart will remember,  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths, steep and stony.  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go ;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them;  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild ;  
Oh ! there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child !  
They arc idids of hearts and of households ,  
They axe angels of God in disguise ;  
And his sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
And his glory still gleams in their eyes.  
Oh ! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild!  
And I know how our Saviour could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
I5ut that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun ;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
Put nir praver would bound back to mvself;  
Ah ! a seraph nny pray for a sinner,  
Rut a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod ;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God .  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction ;  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse the threshold no more;  
Ah ! how shall I sigh for the dear ones,  
That meet me each morn at the door ;  
I shall miss the &quot;good nights&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of iheir innocent glee,  
The gromp on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at evening,-  
Their song in the school and the street ;  
I f-hall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tap of their delicate feet,  
When the lesson and tasks are all ended,  
And death says &quot;the school i dismissed !&quot;  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed!

## [From _The Albion, A Journal of News, Politics and Literature (1822-1876)_](https://archive.org/details/sim_albion-a-journal-of-news-politics-and-literature_1874-01-10_52_2/page/n11/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1874-01-10 &middot; [New York](http://dbpedia.org/resource/New_York_City)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good-night and be kissed ;  
Ol! the little white arms that encircle  
My ne: k in a tender embrace !  
Ob! the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face !  
  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last!  
  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere-the world and its wickedness made me  
  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
Oh! my heart grows as weak as a woman’s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths, steep and stony,  
  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go ;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them ;  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild ;  
Ob! there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart-of a child!  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households ;  
They are angels of God in disguise :  
  
And His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
And His glory still dreams in their eyes.  
  
Oh! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild!  
  
And [know how our Saviour would liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.

## [From _Worcester daily press._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn83021219/1874-01-19/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1874-01-19 &middot; [Worcester, Mass.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Worcester%2C_Massachusetts)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

.  
THE CHILDREN.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good night and be kissed;  
Oh! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh! the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last!  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh! my heart grows as weak as woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths, steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go&#x27;;  
of the mountains of siii hanging o’er them:  
&lt;)f the tempest of fate blowing wild;  
Oh! there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
They arc idols of hearts and of households;  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
And His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
And His glory still dreams in their eyes.  
Oh! those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made more manly and mild!  
And I know how our Saviour could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not for life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done.  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.

When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around uie,  
To bid me good-bye, and be kissed :  
O! the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in the tender embrace,  
OI the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on ay face.  
And when they arc gone, I sit dieaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
^ While it wakes to the pulse of the past  
Ere the world spd its wickedness made uir  
A partner of sorrow and sin;  
When the glory of liod was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
O&#x27; my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountain of feeling will flow.  
When 1 think of the paths sleep and stony.  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go.  
Of the mountains of sin banging o&#x27;er them—  
Ot the tempests of Fate blowing wild,—  
0 &#x27; there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy,  
As the innocent soul of a child.  
Thry are idols of hearts and of household;  
Tuey are angels of liod in disguise;  
Ilis suuligbt still sleeps iu their tresses;

And 1 know now, how Jesus could liken  
The Kingdom uf liod to a child.  
1 ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, aa others have done.  
But that life may have just enough shadow,  
To temper the glare of the snn.  
I would prey liod to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to uiyself.  
Ah 1 a seraph may pray for a sinner.  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
1 have banished tbe roil and tbe ru/«;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge.  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where 1 shut them for breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave tbe old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its shadows no more.  
Ah I how 1 shall sigh for the dear ones  
That met me each morn at the door I

## [From _New York Evangelist (1830-1902)_](https://archive.org/details/sim_evangelist-and-religious-review_1880-01-08_50_2/page/n1/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1880-01-08 &middot; [New York](http://dbpedia.org/resource/New_York_City)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
THE CHILDBEN.  
  
[Poem found In the desk of Chsrlee Dlokens after his death.]  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
  
.Vnd the little ones gather around me  
To bid mo “good-night” and be kissed,  
  
O the little white arms that encircle  
My nock in a tender embrace t  
O the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face I  
  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my ohildnood, too lovely to last;  
  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin—  
  
When the glory of God was about me.  
  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
O my heart grows weak as a woman’s,  
  
And the fountain of feeling will flow.  
  
When I think of the paths, steep and stony.  
  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them.  
  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild—  
  
O there’s nothing on earth half ho holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
  
Thoy are idols of hearts and of households.  
  
They are angels of God in disguise—  
  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses.  
  
His glory still beams in thoir eyes—  
  
O tliose truants from earth and from heaven.  
  
They have made me more manly and mild.  
  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
  
Seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done.  
  
But that life may have Just as mui^ shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun.  
  
I would pray God to guard them from evil.  
  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
  
Ah I a seraph may pray for a sinner.  
  
But a sinner ihust pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
  
I have banished tne rule and the rod;  
  
1 have taught them the goodness of knowledge.  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness.  
  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
  
My frown is sufficient correction.  
  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the Autumn,  
  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
  
Ah 1 how shall 1 sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each mom at the door.  
  
I shall miss the “ good-nights ” and the kisses.  
  
And the gush of their innocent glee.  
  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve.  
  
Their song in the school and the street;  
  
1 shall miss the low hum of their voices.  
  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended.  
  
And Death says the school is dismissed,  
  
May the little ones gather around me.  
  
And bid me “ good-night” and be kissed.

Poetry.  
  
“THE CHILDREN.”  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed,  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming,  
Of my childhood too lovely to last;  
  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
Oh, my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the oy 2 steep and stony  
  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go,  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild;  
Oh, there’s ection of earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise ;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes.  
Oh, those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manful and mild,  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
rhe Kingdom of God to a child.  
  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun. —  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodpess of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction ;  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the

der embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood toe lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin;  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild;  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing of earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes.  
Oh, those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know now how Jesus could liken

All radiant, as others have done,

To temper the glare of the sun.

Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner  
But a sinner must pray for himself.

I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah, how shall I sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door,  
I shall miss the &quot;good-nights&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at noon and at even,  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And Death says, &quot;The school is dismissed!&quot;  
May the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good-night and be kissed!  
Charles Dickens

## [From _The Weekly Oskaloosa herald._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn84027329/1880-09-09/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1880-09-09 &middot; [Oskaloosa, Iowa](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Oskaloosa%2C_Iowa)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

.  
  
I Poem found in the desk of Charles Dick&lt; ns  
after his death.]  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended.  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me &quot;good night&quot; and be kissed.  
Oh the little white arms they encirole,  
My neok in a tender embracel  
Oh the smiles that are halos of Heaven.  
Shedding sunshine&#x27;and love on my face!  
  
And when they are&#x27;gone 1 sit dreaming  
Ot my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When It wakes to the pulse of the past.  
Ere the world and Its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin—  
When the glory of God was about me.  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s.  
And the fountain of feelings will How,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild—  
Oh there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innooent heart of a child 1  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households.  
They are angelsof God In disguise—  
His sunlight still sleeps In their tresses.  
His glory still beams in their eyes—  
Oh those truants from earth ana from Heaven.  
They have made me more manly and mild.  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
  
Seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others hare done.  
But that life may have just as much shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun.  
would prav God toward them tYom evil,  
But my prayers would bound back to sell&#x27;,  
All 1 a seraph may pray for a sinner.  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
1 have banished the rule and the rod;  
1 have taught them the goodness of knowledge  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction.  
My love Is the law of the school.  
1 shall leave the old house In the autumn.  
To traverse Its threshold no more;  
Ah t how shall I sigh lor the dear ones  
That meet each morn at the door.  
I shall miss the &quot;good nights’* and the kisses.  
And the gush of their innocent glee.  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve.  
Their song in the school and the street;  
1 shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended.  
And Death says the school is dismissed.  
May the little ones gather around me.  
And bid me -good night” and be kissed.  
The Voltai

## [THE CHILDREN. (Poem found in the desk of Charles Dickens after his death.)](http://trove.nla.gov.au/ndp/del/article/38263546)

#### From _Launceston Examiner (Tas. : 1842 - 1899)_

#### 1880-10-18 &middot; [Launceston, Tasmania](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Launceston%2C_Tasmania)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

THIE CHILDREN. (Poem found in the desk  
of Charles Dickens after his death.)  
When the lessons and tasks are all  
ended, And the school for the day is  
dismissed, And the little ones gather  
around me To bid me &quot; good night&quot; and be  
kissed. Oh, the little white arms that  
encircle My neck in a tender embrace I  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
;;&#x27; Shedding sunshine and love on my  
face I And when they are gone, I sit  
dreaming Of my childhood, too lovely to  
last; Of love that my heart will  
remember When it wakes to the pulse of  
the past, Ere the world and its  
wickedness made me, A partner of sorrow  
and sinWhen the glory of God was about  
me, And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the-fountain of feelings will flow,  
When I think of the paths, steep and  
stony, Where the feet of the dear ones  
must go ; Of the mountains of sin  
hanging o&#x27;er them, Of the tempests of  
fate blowing wildOh, there&#x27;s nothing on  
earth half so holy As the innocent heart  
of a child. They are idols of hearts and  
of householdsThey are angels of God in  
disguiseHis eunlight still sleeps in  
their tresses, His glory still beams in  
their eyesOh, those truants from earth  
and from heaven, They have made me more  
manly and mild, And I know now how Jesus  
could liken The Kingdom of God to a  
child. Seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done; But  
that life may have just enough shadow To  
temper the glare of the sun. I would  
pray God to guard them from evil, But my  
prayer would bound back to myself ; Ah I  
a seraph may pray for a sinner, But a  
sinner must pray for himself. The twig  
is so easily bended, I have banished the  
rule and the rod ; I have taught them  
the goodness of knowledge, ,They have  
taught me the goodness of God, lly heart  
is a dungeon of darkness, Where I shut  
them from breaking a rule; My frown is  
sufficient correctionMy love is the law  
of the school. I shall leave the old  
house in the autumn To traverse its  
threshold no more; Ah, how shall I sigh  
for the dear ones That meet me each morn  
at the door. I shall miss the &quot; good  
nights&quot; and the kisses, And the gush of  
their innocent glee, The groups on the  
green, and tile flowers That are brought  
every morning to me. I shall miss them  
at morn and at eve, Their song in the  
school and the street, I shall miss the  
low hum of their voices, And the tramp  
of their delicate feet. When the lessons  
and tasks are all ended, And Death says  
the school is dismissed, May the little  
ones gather around me, And bid me &quot; good  
night&quot; and be kissed.

When the lessons and tusks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me &quot;good night&quot; and be kissed;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are hilos of Heaven,  
Shedding sunshine and lore on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember,  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Kre the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
W hen the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as « woman&#x27;s,  
And fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the ieet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin lianging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild;  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothiDg on earth hall so holy  
Ai the innocent heart of a child)

All radiant, as others have done;

To temper the glare of the sun:  
J would pray Goa to guard them from evil;  
But my prayer would bound back to my­  
self;  
Ahl a seraph may prav for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himselt.  
The twig is so e»s:ly bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge.  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where 1 shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
1 shall leave the old house in the Autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more,  
Ahl how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door,  
I shall nuss the good nights and the kistes,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green and the Mowers  
That are brought every morning to me,  
1 shall miss them at mora and at eve,  
Their song in the school and the street,  
1 shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And death says the school is dismissed,  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me &quot;good night&quot; and be kissed.
