## [From _Orleans County monitor._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn84022871/1881-08-22/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1881-08-22 &middot; [Barton, Vt.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Barton%2C_Vermont)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
The following lines were found in the desk of Charles  
Dickens after his death.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended.  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me &quot;Good night,&quot; and bo kissed ;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face !  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming &#x27;  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last ;  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past.  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin  
When the glory of God was about me.  
And the glory of Gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
. And the fountain of feelings will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony;  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the fountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild;  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses.  
His sunlight still beams in their eyes ;  
Oh, those truants from earth and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The Kingdom of God to a child.  
Seek not for a life for the dear ones  
All radiant as others have done.  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun ;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil.  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah ! a seraph may pray for a sinner.  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
When I shut them for breaking a rule,  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the Autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more ;  
Ah 1 how I shall look for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door.  
I shall miss the &quot;Good nights&quot; and the kisses  
And the gush of their innocent glee.  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at noon and at even.  
Their song In the school and the street ;  
I shall miss the hum of their voices.  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And death says the school is dismissed,  
May the little ones gather around me,  
And bid me &quot;Good night&quot; and be kissed.  
Som
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://tile.loc.gov/image-services/iiif/service:ndnp:vtu:batch_vtu_ludlow_ver01:data:sn84022871:00202194400:1881082201:0138/pct:25.509642,13.502688,10.853994,32.476020/!600,600/0/default.jpg"/>

And the li tie ones gather around me.

## [From _The Dillon tribune._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn85053040/1881-12-24/ed-1/?sp=2)

#### 1881-12-24 &middot; [Dillon, Mont.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Dillon%2C_Montana)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

.  
When the lessons and tasks are ail ended.  
And the school for the day is dismissed.  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good-night and be kissed :  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace !  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of Heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to Inst;  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it walces to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
Ana the fountains of feeling will flow  
When I think of the paths steep and stony.  
Where the feet of the deur ones must go;  
Of the mountains ot sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempest of Fate blowing wild;  
Oh, there is nothing on earth half so holv  
As the innocent heart of a child !  
They are idols of heart and of household;  
They are arigels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes :  
Oh, those truents from home and from  
heaven.  
They have made me more man&#x27;v and  
mild,  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
I ask not a life for the dear ones  
All radient, as others have done.  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun ;  
I pray God t&lt; guard them from evil,  
But my prrver would bound back toniv­  
self;  
Ah ! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must ptay for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod ;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowl­  
edge,  
They have taught me the goodness of  
God;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness.  
Where I shut them for breaking a rule ;  
My frown is sufficient correction :  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn.  
To traverse Us threshold no more:&#x27;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the deal ones.  
That meet me each morn at tne dooi !  
I shall miss the &quot;good-nighls&quot; and the  
kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee.  
The group of the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve,  
Their song in the school and the street ;  
I shall miss the low hum of the voices.  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended.  
And death says, &quot;The school is dis­  
missed!&quot;  
Mny the little ones gather around me.  
To bid me good-night and be kissed.

## [From _Journal of Education 1875-2015_](https://archive.org/details/sim_journal-of-education_1882-07-13_16_378/page/n2/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1882-07-13 &middot; [Boston, Massachusetts](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Boston)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
FOUND IN THE DESK OF CHARLES DICKENS AFTER HIS  
DEATH,  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good night and be kissed,  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Ob, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face!  
  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last,  
  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the love of the past;  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was above me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman’s,  
And fountains of sorrow will flow,  
  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempests of fate growing wild;  
  
Oh, there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise,  
His sunlight still sleeps on their tresses,  
His glory still beams in their eyes;  
Oh, those truants from earth and from Heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
  
Seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done;  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back on myself;  
Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
  
I have banished the rule and the rod:  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
  
ere I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
y love is the law of the school.  
  
i shall leave the old home in autumn  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That met me each morn at the door!  
  
I shall miss the good-night and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee;  
  
The group on the green, and the flowers,  
They are brought every morning to me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve,  
Their song in the school and the street;  
shall m low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
ys is dismissed,  
ones around me  
  
— The Teacher’s Companion.
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://iiif.archive.org/image/iiif/2/sim_journal-of-education_1882-07-13_16_378%2Fsim_journal-of-education_1882-07-13_16_378_jp2.zip%2Fsim_journal-of-education_1882-07-13_16_378_jp2%2Fsim_journal-of-education_1882-07-13_16_378_0002.jp2/pct:8.062235,34.123037,26.131542,50.876963/,600/0/default.jpg"/>
</td>
</tr></table>

My heart grows as weak as a woman’s,  
And the fount of my feelings will flow,  
When I think of the path steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the loved ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin growing o’er them,  
Of the tempest of fate growing wild;  
For there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of the child.

## [THE CHILDREN. FOUND IN THE DESK OF CHARLES DICKENS AFTER HIS DEATH.](http://trove.nla.gov.au/ndp/del/article/90574338)

#### From _The Bacchus Marsh Express (Vic. : 1866 - 1918)_

#### 1883-06-09 &middot; [Bacchus Marsh, Victoria](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Bacchus_Marsh)

THE CHILDREN. FOUND IN TUE DESK OF  
CHARLES DICKENs AFTER me DEATH. When the  
lessons and tasks are all ended, And the  
school for the day is dismissed, And the  
little ones gather around me To&#x27;bid me  
&quot;good night&quot; and bek hissed; Oh, the

and love on my face! And when they are

willremember, When it wakes to the pulse

and mild, And I know how Jesus could  
liken The kingdom of God to a child.  
Seek not a life for the dear ones All  
radiant, as others have done; But that  
life may have just as much shadow To  
temper the glare of the sun: I would  
pray God to guard them from evil, But my  
prayer would bound back to myself; Ah !  
a seraph may pray for a sinner But a  
sinner must pray for himself. The twig  
is so easily bonded, I have banished the

me the goodness of God. My heart is a  
dungeon of darkness. Whence I shut them  
for breaking the rule; My frown is  
sufficient correction, My love is the  
law of the school. I shall leave the old  
house in the autumn, To travel its  
threshold no more, Ah ! how I shall sigh  
for the dear ones That met me each morn  
at the door, I shall miss the good  
nights and the kisses, And the gush sI

And the tramp of their delicate feet.

THE CHILDREN.  
  
“When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
“To bid me * Good night” and be kissed,  
©, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck ina tender embrace!  
0, the smiles that are haloes of Heaven,  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face!  
And when they are gone [ sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulee of the past,  
Bre the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin—  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
© wy heart grows weak as 8 woman’s,  
And the fountain of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild—  
@, there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
They are idols of heart andof household,  
They are angels of Godin dieguise—  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still beams in their eyes—  
©, those truants from earth and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And [ know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
Seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant as others have done,  
But that life may have just as much shadow,  
To temper the glare of the sun.  
4 would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself,  
Ah! aseraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and tbe rod;  
Z have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
&quot;They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse the threshold no more;  
Ab! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door.  
I shall miss the “Good nights” and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
JI shall miss them at morn and at eve,  
Their song in the school and the street;  
T shall miss the low hum of their veices,

## [From _The Pacific._](https://archive.org/details/per_the-pacific_the-pacific_1884-07-23_33_30/page/n5/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1884-07-23 &middot; [San Francisco [Calif.]](http://dbpedia.org/resource/San_Francisco)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
Children’s Corner.  
  
The Children.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me ‘‘good-night’’ and be kissed—  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face!  
  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them,  
  
‘Of the tempests of fate blowing wild—  
  
Oh, there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still beams in their eyes.  
Oh, those tyrants from earth and from  
heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child!  
  
Seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done;  
  
But that life may have just as much shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun.  
  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to my-  
  
self;  
  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig 1s so easily bended,  
  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowl-  
  
edge;  
  
They taught me the goodness of  
My heart is 2 dungeon of darkness,  
  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more.  
  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door.  
  
I shall miss the gcod-nights and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
  
The group on the green and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve,  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And Death says the school is dismissed,  
May the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good night and be kissed.  
—Charles Dickens.

## [THE CHILDREN. [Poem found in the desk of Charles Dickens after his death and republished by request.]](http://trove.nla.gov.au/ndp/del/article/160100754)

#### From _Adelaide Observer (SA : 1843 - 1904)_

#### 1884-09-06 &middot; [Adelaide, South Australia](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Adelaide)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

THE CHILDREN. [Poem found in the desk of  
Charles Dickens after his death and  
republished by request.] When the  
lessons and tasks are all ended, And the  
school tor the day is dismissed, And  
the&#x27; little ones gather aronnd me To bid  
me &quot;good night&quot; and be kissed— Oh the  
little white arms that encircle My neck  
in a tender embrace 1 Oh the smiles that  
are balos of heaven, Shedding sunshine  
and love on my face I And when they are  
gone, I sit dreaming Of my childhood,  
too lovely to last Of love that my heart  
will remember When it wakes to the poise  
of the past, Ere the world and its  
wickedness made me A partner of sorrow  
and sin When the glory of God was ahont  
me And the glory of gladness within, Ob  
my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s And the  
fountain of feeling will flow, When I  
think of the path steep and stony, Where  
the feet of the dear ones mast go; Of  
the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wildOb  
there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy As  
the innocent heart of a child. They are  
idols of hearts and of households, They  
are angels of God in disguise— His  
sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still beams in their eyes. Oh  
those truants from earth and from  
heaven, They have made me more manly and  
mild, And I know now how Jesus could  
liken The Kingdom of God to a child.  
Seek not a life for the dear ones All  
radiant, as others have done: But that  
life may have just as much shadow To  
temper the glare of the sun. I would  
pray God to guard them from evil, But my  
prayer would bound back tomyself; Ah i a  
seraph may pray for a sinner, But a  
sinner must pray for himself. The twig  
is so easily bended, I have banished the  
rule and the rod; I have taught them the  
goodness of knowledge, They have taught  
me the goodness of God. Mv heart is a  
dungeon of darkness, Where I shut them  
for breaking a rule ; My frown is  
sufficient correction, My love is the  
law of the school. I shall leave the old  
bouse in the autumn, To traverse its  
threshold no more; Ah! how shall I sigh  
for the dear ones That meet me each morn  
at the door. I shall miss the &quot;good  
nights&quot; andthekisses, And the gush of  
their innocent glee, The group on the  
green, and the flowers That are brought  
every morning to me. I shall miss them  
at morn and at eve, Their song in the  
school and the street; I shall miss the  
low hum of their voices, And the tramp  
of their delicate feet. When the lessons  
and tasks are all ended. And Death says  
the school is dismissed, May the little  
ones gather around me. And bid me &quot;  
good-night&quot; and be kissed.

THE CHILDREN. (Found in the Desk of

When ihe lessons and tasks are all  
ended, And tbe school for the day ia  
dismissed, And the little ones gather  
around me ? To bid ine good-night and be  
kissed ; &#x27; Oh, tlie little white arms  
that encircle My neck in a tender  
embrace ! Oh, the smiles that are balos  
of heaven, Shedding sunshine and love on  
my face ! ? And when they are gone I sit

last, Of love that my heart will  
remember When it wakes to tbe love of  
tbe past; Ere the -world and its  
wickedness made me A partner of sorrow  
and tin ; When the glory of God was  
above me, &#x27; And the glory of gladness  
within, Oh, my heart grows weak as a  
woman&#x27;s, And fountains of sorrow will  
flow. When I think of the paths eteep  
and stony Where tbe feet of the dear  
ones must go ; Of the mountains of sin  
hanging- o&#x27;er them, Of the tempests of  
fate growing wild ; Oh, there&#x27;s nothing  
oa earth half so holy As the innocent  
heart of a child ! Tney are idols of  
hearts and of households, &#x27; They are  
angels of God iu disguise, His sunlight  
still sleeps on their tresses, His glory  
still beams in their eyes ; Oh, those  
taunts from earth and from Heaven, They

know how Jesus could liken The kingdom  
of God to a. child. Ssek not a life for  
the dear ones All radiant, as others  
have done; But that life may have just  
enough shadow To temper the glare of the  
sun ; I would pray God to guard them  
from evil, But my prayer would bound  
back on myself;  Ah, a seraph may pray  
for a Burner, But a sinner must pray for  
nimsnlf. : The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod ; I  
have taught them tbe goodness of  
knowledge, They have taught me the  
goodness of God. My heart is a dungeon  
of darkness, Where I shut them from  
breaking a sole ; -. My frown is  
sufficient correction, My love is the  
law of the school. I shall leave the old  
home in tiie autumn, To traverse its  
threshold no more ; Ah ! how I shall  
sigu for the dear ones That meet me each  
morn at the door ! I shall miss the  
good-night and the kisses, And tbe gush  
of their innocent glee ; : The group on  
tbe green, and tbe flowers, -They are  
brought every morning to me. . . I shall  
miss them at morn and at even, Their  
song in the school and the street ; I  
shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tramp of their delicate feat. &#x27;  
When the lessons and tasks are all  
ended, And Death says school is  
dismissed, May the little ones gather  
around me, To bid me good-sight and be  
kissed.

## The Children

#### From _Rocky Mountain news._

## [From _The American Magazine 1884-1888_](https://archive.org/details/sim_american-magazine_1885-03_1_6/page/n13/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1885-03-01 &middot; [New York City, New York](http://dbpedia.org/resource/New_York_City)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

. DICKINSON.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed :  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace !  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last :  
  
Of joy, that my heart will remember,  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me,  
  
A partner of sorrow and sin ;  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
All my heart grows as weak as a woman’s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of Sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempest of Fate blowing wild ;  
Oh, there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child !  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households ;  
They are angels of God in disguise ;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes.  
Those truants from home and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun ;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself ;  
Ah ! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banish&#x27;d the rule and the rod ;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God ;  
My heart is the dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them for breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction ;  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more ;  
Ah ! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door ;  
I shall miss the “‘ good-nights” and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning for me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at even,  
Their song in the school and the street ;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tread of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons of life are all ended,  
And Death says, ‘‘ The school is dismissed !”  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night, and be kiss’d !
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://iiif.archive.org/image/iiif/2/sim_american-magazine_1885-03_1_6%2Fsim_american-magazine_1885-03_1_6_jp2.zip%2Fsim_american-magazine_1885-03_1_6_jp2%2Fsim_american-magazine_1885-03_1_6_0013.jp2/pct:11.305361,15.315513,25.903263,60.780018/,600/0/default.jpg"/>
</td>
</tr></table>

## [From _The Vermont watchman._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn86071719/1885-04-01/ed-1/?sp=3)

#### 1885-04-01 &middot; [Montpelier, Vt.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Montpelier%2C_Vermont)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

:  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
Then the little ones gather around me  
To bid me &quot;good night&quot; and be kissed.  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love, that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go,  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild;  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise,  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still beams in their eyes;  
  
Oh, those truants from earth and from heaven,  
  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
I seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just as much shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn  
To traverse its threshold no more  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That me

e  
  
THE CHILDREY.  
  
Found in the desk of Charles Dickens  
  
after his death.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended.  
  
And the school for the day is dismissed  
  
And the little ones gathered around me  
  
To bid me &quot;good night&quot; and be kissed:  
  
Oh, the little white hands that encircle  
  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face!  
  
And when they are gone I am dreaming,  
  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
  
Of love, that my heart will remember  
  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
  
Ere the world and its wickedness made  
  
mlle  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
  
When the glory of God was about me,  
  
And the glory of gladness within,  
  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
  
And the fountain of feeling will flow,  
  
When I think of the path steep and stony,  
  
Where the feet of the dear ones must  
  
go,  
  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er  
  
them,  
  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild;  
  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth halt so holy,  
  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
  
They are idols of hearts and of house  
  
holds,  
  
They are angels of God in disguise  
  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
  
His glory still beams in their eyes;  
  
Oh, those truants from earth and from  
  
heaven  
  
They have made me more manly and  
  
mild  
  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
  
Seek not a life for the dear ones  
  
All radiant as others have done.  
  
But that life may have just as much  
  
shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun:  
  
I would pray God to guard them from  
  
evil,  
  
But my prayer would bound back to  
  
myself;  
  
Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
  
I have banished the rule and the rod  
  
I have taught them the goodness of  
  
knowlege  
  
They have taught me the goodness of  
  
God.  
  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
  
Where I shut them from breaking a  
  
rule  
  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn  
  
To traverse its old threshold no more  
  
Ah, how shall I sigh for the dear one  
  
That meet me each morn at the door,  
  
I shall miss the &quot;good-nights&quot; and the  
  
kisses  
  
And the gash of their innocent glee,  
  
The group on the green, and the flowers  
  
That are brought every morning to me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve,  
  
Their song in the school and the street  
  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices  
  
And the tramp of their delicate feet  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended  
  
And death says the school is dismissed,  
  
May the little ones gather around me  
  
To bid me &quot;goed-night&quot; and be kissed  
  
Charles Dicken

THE CHILDREN. A correspondent says the  
following beautiful lines were found in  
the desk of Charles Dickens after his  
death. Independent of their intrinsic  
beauty, they show how tender the heart  
of the great novelist was towards  
children : — When the lessons and tasks

is dismissed, Ana tne utue ones gatner  
arouna me To bid me good-night and be  
kissed ; Ob, the little white arms that

Oh. the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding eu&amp;sjune and lore on my face 1  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming Of  
my childhood, too lovely to last, Of  
love that my heart will remember When it  
wakes *-o Che lore of the past ; Ere the  
world and its wickedness made me A  
partner of sorrow and sin. When the  
glory of God ra« above me, And the glory  
of gladness within. Oh, my heart grows  
weak as a woman&#x27;s, And fountains of  
sorrow will flow, When I think of the  
paths steep and stony Where the feet of  
tbe dear ones mnei go ; Of the mountains  
of sin hanging o&#x27;er diem, Of the  
tempests of fate growing wlid; Oh,  
there&#x27;s nothing- on earth hal &#x27; so holy

are idols of hearts and of households,

sunlight ctilj sleeps on their tresses,

the autumn, To traverse its threshold no  
more — Ah, how 1 shall sigh for the dear  
ones That meet me each morn at the door.  
I shall miss the good-nights and the  
kisses, And the gush of their innocent  
glee, The group on the green and the  
flowers That are brought every morning  
to me. 1 shall miss them at morn and at  
eve, Their song in the school and the  
street, I shall miss the low hum of  
their voices And the tramp of their  
delicate feet. When the lessons and  
tasks are all ended, And death says the  
school is dismissed, Mav the little ones  
gather around me To bid me &#x27; Good-night&#x27;  
and be kissed. Charles Dicken

## [From _The Atlanta constitution._](https://archive.org/details/per_atlanta-constitution_1885-12-28_18/page/n4/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1885-12-28 &middot; [Atlanta, Ga.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Atlanta)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
‘My heart grows weak as a woman’s  
And the tountains of feeling will flow,  
WhenI think of the path, steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging over them;  
Of the tempest of fate blowing wild.  
Ch! there is nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
  
“These idols of our hearts and households!  
They are angels of God in disguise.  
  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses;  
His glory still lingers in their eves.  
  
Oh! these blessings trom God and from heaven!  
They make us more tender and mild!  
  
And we see how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God toa child.”

## [From _The Hawaiian gazette._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn83025121/1886-01-12/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1886-01-12 &middot; [Honolulu [Oahu, Hawaii]](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Honolulu)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
The School Teacher&#x27;s Reveri  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended  
And the school for the day is dismissed  
d the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good-night and be kissed  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven  
Shedding sunshine and love on my fac  
And when they are goue I sit dreaming  
Of my childhoed, too lovely to last  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the love of the past  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin  
When the glory of God was above me  
And the glory of gladness within  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s  
And fountains of sorrow will flow  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
here the feet of the dear ones must go  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them  
Of the tempest of fate growing wild  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child  
They are idols of hearts and of houscholds,  
They are angels of God in disguise,  
His sunlight still slecps on their tresses  
His glory still beams in their eyes  
Oh, those truants from carth and from heaven  
They have made me more manly and mild  
And I now know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child  
I seck not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun  
I would pray God to guard them from evil  
But my prayer would bound back on myself  
Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner  
But a sininer must pray for himself  
The twig is so easily bended  
I have banished the rule and the rod  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge  
have taught me the goodness of God  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule  
My frown is sufficient correction  
ly love is the law of the school  
I shall leave the old home in the antumn  
To traverse its threshold no more  
Ah! how shall I sigh for the dear ones  
That mect me cach morn at the door  
I shall miss the good-night and the kisses  
And the gush of their innocent glee  
The group on the green, and the flower  
That are brought every morning to m  
I shall miss them at morn and at even  
Their song in the school and the street  
I shall miss the low hum of their voice  
And the tramp of their delicate feet  
hen the lessons and tasks are all ended  
And Death says school is dismissed  
May the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good-night and be kissed  
Charles Dicken

## [From _The Hawaiian gazette._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn83025121/1886-01-12/ed-1/?sp=2)

#### 1886-01-12 &middot; [Honolulu [Oahu, Hawaii]](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Honolulu)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
The School Teacher&#x27;s Reverie  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended  
And the school for the day is dismissed  
nd the little ones gather around me  
To bid me good-night and be kissed  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the love of the past  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin  
When the glory of God was above me  
And the glory of gladness within  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s  
And fountains of sorrow will flow  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them  
Of the tempest of fate growing wild  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child  
They are idols of hearts and of household  
They are angels of God in disguise  
His sunlight still sleeps on their tresse  
His glory still beams in their eyes  
Oh, those truants from earth and from heaven  
They have made me more manly and mild  
And I now know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child!  
I seek not a life for the dear one  
  
All radiant, as others have done  
  
But that life may have just enough shadow

I have banished the rule and the rod  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge  
They have taught me the goodness of God  
My heart is a dungeon of darknes  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule  
My frown is sufficient correction  
My love is the law of the school  
I shall leave the old home in the antumn  
To traverse its threshold no more  
Ah! how shall I sigh for the dear ones

## [From _The Vermont watchman._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn86071719/1887-06-22/ed-1/?sp=3)

#### 1887-06-22 &middot; [Montpelier, Vt.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Montpelier%2C_Vermont)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
Little Children.  
The following beautiful little poem, from  
the pen of Charles Dickens, was found in  
his desk after his death:  
When the lessons and tasks are ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me &quot;good-night&quot; and be kissed;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love, that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me  
And the glory of gladness within.  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountain of feeling will flow  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild;  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
They are idols of hearts and of household,  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still beams in their eyes;  
Oh, those truants from earth and from heaven,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child.  
Seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done.  
But that life may have just as much shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun.  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah, a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them from breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction,  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more  
Ah, how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet 
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://tile.loc.gov/image-services/iiif/service:ndnp:vtu:batch_vtu_graniteville_ver01:data:sn86071719:00280777699:1887062201:0616/pct:4.067352,6.571429,14.410671,26.528571/!600,600/0/default.jpg"/>

## [From _Pawtucket record._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn92064062/1887-11-15/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1887-11-15 &middot; [Pawtucket, R.I.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Pawtucket%2C_Rhode_Island)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

Y.  
  
Pocetry,  
  
The Children.  
  
FOUND IN THE DESK OF CHARLES DICKEN  
AFTER HIS DEATH.  
  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
And the little ones gather around me  
To bid me * good-night,” and be kissed;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in a tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine and love on my face!  
  
And when they are gone, I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last;  
Of love that my heart will remember  
When it wakes to the pulse of the past,  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
Oh, my heart grows weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountains of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempests of fate blowing wild;  
Oh, there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child.  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households,  
They are angels of God in disguise,  
His sunlight stili sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still beams in their eyes;  
Oh, those truants from earth and from heaven!  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of heaven to a child.  
  
Seek not a life for the dear ones  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just as much shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself!  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God.  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness  
Where I shut them from breaking the rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction;  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn  
To traverse its threshold no more—  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door,  
I shall miss the good-nights and the kisses  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The group on the green and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me,  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at eve,  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices  
And the tramp of their delicate feet,  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And Death says the school is dismissed,  
May the little ones gather around me  
To bid me ** good-night,” and be kissed!  
  
THINGS WORTH
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">

</tr></table>

## [From _Current Literature (1888-1912)_](https://archive.org/details/sim_current-opinion_1889-06_2_6/page/n50/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1889-06-01 &middot; [New York](http://dbpedia.org/resource/New_York_City)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

n  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed  
O, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace!  
O, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face:  
  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood too lovely to last,—  
Of joy that my heart will remember,  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past;  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
  
All my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountain of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go,—  
Of the mountains of Sin hanging o’er them,  
Of the tempest of Fate blowing wild,—  
O, there’s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households ;  
They are angels of God in disguise ;  
  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still shines in their eyes ;  
  
Those truants from home and from heaven—  
They have made me more manly and mild;  
  
And I know now, how JESUS could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child  
  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun ;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself :  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod,  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them for breaking a rule:  
My frown is sufficient correction ;  
My love is the law of the school.  
  
I shall leave the old house in the Autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more ;  
  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones,  
That meet me each morn at the door ;  
  
I shall miss the “ good nights ” and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
  
The groups on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
  
I shall miss them at morn and at even,  
Their song in the school and the street ;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tread of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons of life are all ended,  
And Death says, “ The schoo] is dismissed !  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good-night and be kissed!

## Who Wrote "The Children"

## [From _Middlebury register._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn93063557/1889-07-12/ed-1/?sp=2)

#### 1889-07-12 &middot; [Middlebury, Vt.](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Middlebury%2C_Vermont)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
WHO WROTE &quot;THE CHIHLOREN.&quot;  
  
A Letter from the Son of Charles Dicken  
That Ends an Old Controversy.  
There is scarcely a reader of English verse  
who has not read and admired the following  
poem, by Charles M. Dickinson, the editor of  
The Binghamton Republican. It has been  
printed again and again in American and Eng­  
lish newspapers, in many school books, and  
in nearly all collections of verse. The poem  
has been invariably credited to the author in  
books, but for several years it bas been  
widely printed in the newspapers over the  
name of Charles Dickens. Mr. Dickinson  
now gives to the public the following note  
from the son of the dead novelist  
HoteL Brunswick, NeW York,  
  
DEAR SIR-In reply to the letter which  
William Henry Smith has been good enough  
to forward to me, I willingly testify to the  
fact that the poem, &quot;The Children,&quot; which  
has so often been erroneously attributed to  
my father, was not  
written by him;  
and that, far from  
having claimed it  
as his, I have writ­  
ten during the last  
seventeen years a  
large number of  
letters, and have  
many times insert-  
ed in my magazine,  
Household Words,  
answers to corre­  
spondents stating  
that the story about  
the poem having  
been found in my  
father&#x27;s desk after  
his death was en  
tirely apocryphal, ChArLEs M. Dickinson.  
and that I was altogether unaware to whom  
the credit of the authorship of the verses was  
due. I am, dear sir, faithfully yours,  
CHARLES DICKENS.  
Charles M. Dickinson, Esq., Daily Repubk-  
can, Binghamton, N. Y.  
Cassell &amp; Co., New York, and Sampson  
Low, Marston &amp; Co., London, have just is­  
sued a very handsome volume of Mr. Dick­  
inson&#x27;s hitherto unpublished verse. The  
poem, &quot;The Children,&quot; over which there has  
been such a dispute, is as follows:  
THE CHILDREN.  
When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace!  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face!  
And when they are gone I sit dreaming  
Of my childhood, too lovely to last  
Of joy that my heart will remember,  
While it wakes to the pulse of the past;  
Ere the world and its wickedness made me  
A partner of sorrow and sin,  
When the glory of God was about me,  
And the glory of gladness within.  
All my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s,  
And the fountain of feeling will flow,  
When I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of the dear ones must go  
Of the mountains of Sin hanging o&#x27;er them,  
Of the tempest of Fate blowing wild  
Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy  
As the innocent heart of a child!  
They are idols of hearts and of households;  
They are angels of God in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
His glory still gleams in their eyes;  
Those truants from home and from heaven  
They have made me more manly and mild;  
And I know now how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of God to a child!  
I ask not a life for the dear ones,  
All radiant, as others have done,  
But that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray God to guard them from evil,  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner,  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God;  
My heart is a dungeon of darkness,  
Where I shut them for breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction;  
My love is the law of the school.  
I shall leave the old house in the autumn,  
To traverse its threshold no more;  
Ah! how I shall sigh for the dear ones,  
That meet me each morn at the door;  
I shall miss the &quot;good nights&quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee,  
The greups on the green, and the flowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at even,  
Their song in the school and the street;  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
And the tread of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons of life are all ended,  
And death says, &quot;The school is dismissed!&quot;  
May the little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed!  
The VIrgINia Railroad Accident.  
The recent accident on the Norfolk and  
Western railroad in Richmond, in which a  
train ran into a wash out, was one of the  
most destructive to life and property of the  
year. The cut accompanying this is from a  
sketch made for The Philadelphia Press by  
George Masters, civil engineer, of Philadel  
phia, who was a passenger on the wrecked  
train.
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">
<img alt="Page image" src="https://tile.loc.gov/image-services/iiif/service:ndnp:vtu:batch_vtu_irasburg_ver01:data:sn93063557:00280777869:1889071201:1056/pct:51.395298,4.969512,14.919798,72.698171/!600,600/0/default.jpg"/>
</td>
</tr></table>

## [From _The Academy and Literature 1869-1916_](https://archive.org/details/sim_academy-and-literature_1889-09-14_36_906/page/n6/mode/1up?view=theater)

#### 1889-09-14 &middot; [London, England](http://dbpedia.org/resource/London)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

 to the poet, and for the  
rest to the children who, as we read them, seem  
to inspire them :  
  
‘© When the lessons and tasks are all ended,  
And the school for the day is dismissed,  
The little ones gather around me,  
To bid me good night and be kissed ;  
Oh, the little white arms that encircle  
My neck in their tender embrace !  
Oh, the smiles that are halos of heaven,  
Shedding sunshine of love on my face !  
+ * * * *  
  
“* The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod ;  
I havo taught them the goodness of knowledge,  
They have taught me the goodness of God ;  
My heart is the dungeon of darkness  
Where I shut them for breaking a rule;  
My frown is sufficient correction ;  
My love is the Jaw of the school.”
</td><td style="width: 50%; max-height: 75%; margin: auto; display: block;">

## [From _Belmont chronicle._](https://www.loc.gov/resource/sn85026241/1890-06-12/ed-1/?sp=1)

#### 1890-06-12 &middot; [St. Clairsville, Ohio](http://dbpedia.org/resource/St._Clairsville%2C_Ohio)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

  
  
THE CHILDREN.  
  
They are idols of hearts and of households;  
They are angels of Ood in disguise;  
His sunlight still sleeps in their tresses.  
His glory still shines in their eyes.  
Those truants from home and from heaven  
They have made me more manly and mild.  
And I know how Jesus could liken  
The kingdom of Ood to a child.  
I ask not a life for the dear ones  
All radient as others have done.  
And that life may have just enough shadow  
To temper the glare of the sun;  
I would pray tiod to guard them from evil.  
But my prayer would bound back to myself;  
Ah! a seraph may pray for a sinner.  
But a sinner must pray for himself.  
The twig is so easily bended,  
I have banished the rule and the rod;  
I have taught them the goodness of knowledge.  
They taught me the goodness of Ood;  
My heart is the dungeon of darkness  
Where I shut them for breaking a luic;  
My frown is suDicient correction;  
My love is the law of the schooL  
I shall leave the house In the autumn.  
To traverse the threshold no more;  
Ah, how shall I sigh for the dear ones  
That meet me each morn at the door.  
I shall miss the &quot; good night &quot; and the kisses,  
And the gush of their innocent glee.  
The group on the green and the (lowers  
That are brought every morning to me.  
I shall miss them at morn and at even.  
Their song in the school and the street,  
I shall miss the low hum of their voices,  
Aud he tread of their delicate feet.  
When the lessons of life are all ended.  
And death says &quot;The school is dismissed! &#x27;  
May the little ones gather around me, -  
Aud bid me good night and be kissed.  
  
Charle M. Dickinson.

glory of God was about me, And the glory  
of gladness within. Oh, my heart grows  
as weak as a woman&#x27;s, And the fountain  
of feelings will flow, When I think of  
the paths steop and stony, Where the  
feet of my dear ones must so; Of tile  
mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er them, Of  
the tempests of fate blowing wild ; Oh,  
there&#x27;s nothing on earth half so holy As  
the innocent heart of a child. They are  
idols of hearts and of households, They  
are angels of God in disguise — His  
sunlight still sleeps in their tresses,  
HiB glory still beams in their eyes ;  
Oh, those truants from earth and from  
Heaven, They have made me more manly and  
mild, And I know now how Jesus could  
liken The Kingdom of God to a child. ,  
Seek not a life for the dear ones All  
radiant, as others have done, But that  
life may have just as much shadow To  
temper the glare of the sun ; I would  
pray God to guard them from - evil, But  
my prayer would bound back to myself; ,  
Ah I a seraph may pray for a sinner, But  
a sinner must pray for himself. The twig  
is so easily bended, I have banished the  
rnle and the rod ; I have taught them  
the &#x27;goodness of knowledge, They have  
taught me the goodness of God. My heart  
is a dungeon of darkness, Where I shut  
them for breaking a rule ; My frown is  
sufficient conviction, My love is the  
law of the school. I shall leave the old  
house in the autumn. To traverse its  
threshold no more ; Ah ! how I shall  
sigh for the dear ones That met me each  
morn at the door. I shall miss the &#x27;  
Good nights &#x27; and the kisses, ,. ; And

## [The Children. [Found in the desk of Charles Dickens after his death, and supposed to be the only poem ever written by the "Master."]](http://trove.nla.gov.au/ndp/del/article/31370527)

#### From _Queanbeyan Age (NSW : 1867 - 1904)_

#### 1899-12-23 &middot; [Queanbeyan, New South Wales](http://dbpedia.org/resource/Queanbeyan)

<table style="width: 100%;"><tr><td style="width: 50%">

The Children. By Charles Dickens. [Found  
in the desk of Charles Dickens after his  
death, and supposed to be the only poem  
ever written by the &quot;Master.&quot;] &amp;nbsp;  
When the lessons and tasks are all  
ended, And the school for the day is  
dismissed, And the little ones gather  
around me, To bid me &quot;Good night &quot; and  
be kissed; Oh ! the little white arms  
that encircle My neck in a tender  
embrace ! Oh, the smiles that are halos  
of Heaven, Shedding sunshine and love on  
my face ! And when they are gone I am  
dreaming Of my childhood, too lovely to  
last ; Of love that my heart will  
remember When it wakes to a pulse of the  
past; Ere the world and its wickedness  
made me. A partner of sorrow and sin--  
When the glory of God was about me, And  
the glory of gladness within. &amp;nbsp; Oh,  
my heart grows as weak as a woman&#x27;s, And  
the fountain of feelings will flow, When  
I think of the paths steep and stony,  
Where the feet of my dear ones must go ;  
Of the mountains of sin hanging o&#x27;er  
them, Of the tempests of fate blowing  
wild; Oh, there&#x27;s nothing on earth half  
so holy &amp;nbsp; As the innocent heart of  
a child. They are idols, of hearts and  
of &amp;nbsp; households, &amp;nbsp; They are  
angels of God in disguiseHis sunlight  
still sleeps in their tresses, His glory  
still beams in their eyes ; Oh, those  
truants from earth and from Heaven ,  
They have made me more manly and mild,  
And I know now how Jesus could liken The  
Kingdom of God to a child. Seek not a  
life for the dear ones All radiant, as  
others have done, But that life may have  
just as much shadow To temper the glare  
of the sun ; I would pray God to guard  
them from evil, But my prayer would  
bound back to myself; Ah ! a seraph may  
pray for a sinner, But a sinner must  
pray for himself. The twig is so easily  
bended, I have banished the rule and the  
rod ; I have taught them the goodness of  
knowledge, They have taught me the  
goodness of God. My heart is a dungeon  
of darkness, Where I shut them for  
breaking a rule; My frown is sufficient  
conviction, My love is the law of the  
school. I shall leave the old house in  
the autumn, &amp;nbsp; To traverse its  
threshold no more ; Ah ! how I shall  
sigh for the dear ones That met me each  
morn at the door. I shall miss the &quot;Good  
nights&quot; and the kisses, And the gush of  
their innocent glee, The group on the  
green, and the flowers That are brought  
every morning to me . I shall miss them  
at morn and at even, Their songs in the  
school and the street, I shall miss the  
low hum of their voices, And the tramp  
of their delicate feet. When the lessons  
and tasks are all ended, And death says,  
&quot; the school is dismissed, &quot; May the  
little ones gather around me, And bid me  
&quot; Good night&quot; and be kissed.
</td></tr></table>
